- A string containing the text (e.g., a passage from Tolstoy or Dostoevsky).
- A list of strings representing the thematic words to track (e.g., ["freedom", "soul", "fate"]).

- A dictionary with the thematic words as keys and their counts in the text as values.

```python

```

1. Count the occurrences of each thematic word in the text, case-insensitively.

Iteration 26: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task Instruction for Assistant

## Task Overview
You are to write a Python function that extracts and counts the number of unique email domains from a list of email addresses. This task is relevant to data analysis in marketing, particularly when segmenting audiences based on email service providers. The function should be efficient, readable, and meet all specified constraints.

## Input Format
- A list of email addresses (strings). For example: `['user1@gmail.com', 'user2@yahoo.com', 'user3@gmail.com', 'user4@outlook.com']`.

## Output Format
- An integer representing the number of unique email domains in the list.

## Constraints
1. The function must return the correct count of unique domains.
2. All email addresses are assumed to be valid and in lowercase.
3. The function must be well-documented with a docstring that explains its purpose, parameters, and return value.
4. The response must include **at least two sections highlighted with markdown**, such as `*highlighted section*`.
5. The function must be written in Python and use best practices for clarity and efficiency.
6. The assistant must ensure that the function is generalizable and can handle edge cases, such as empty lists or duplicate domains.

## Additional Guidelines
- The function should split each email address at the `@` character to isolate the domain part.
- The function should use a `set` to automatically handle uniqueness.
- The function should return the length of the set to provide the count of unique domains.
- The assistant should highlight the use of `set` for uniqueness and the method of splitting the email to extract the domain as the two highlighted sections.
- The assistant should ensure that the code is clean, readable, and follows PEP8 guidelines.

## Example
For the input `['user1@gmail.com', 'user2@yahoo.com', 'user3@gmail.com', 'user4@outlook.com']`, the output should be `3` because there are three unique domains: `gmail.com`, `yahoo.com`, and `outlook.com`.

## Domain-Specific Information
- Email domains are typically the part of the email address that comes after the `@` symbol.
- In marketing and customer data analysis, understanding email domains can help segment users based on their email service providers, which can inform targeted advertising strategies.
- The function is useful for analyzing customer data and tailoring digital advertising strategies, especially in markets like Asia where email usage patterns can vary by provider.

## Generalizable Strategy
- Use a `set` to store unique domains, as it automatically handles duplicates.
- Split each email address at the `@` symbol to extract the domain.
- Return the length of the set to get the number of unique domains.

## Final Instructions
Write a Python function that meets all the above requirements. Ensure that your response includes at least two highlighted sections, and that the code is well-documented and follows best practices.

Iteration 28: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task Instruction for Assistant

## Task Overview
You are to write a Python function that extracts and counts the number of unique email domains from a list of email addresses. This task is relevant to data analysis in marketing, particularly when segmenting audiences based on email service providers. The function should be efficient, readable, and meet all specified constraints.

## Input Format
- A list of email addresses (strings). For example: `['user1@gmail.com', 'user2@yahoo.com', 'user3@gmail.com', 'user4@outlook.com']`.

## Output Format
- An integer representing the number of unique email domains in the list.

## Constraints
1. The function must return the correct count of unique domains.
2. All email addresses are assumed to be valid and in lowercase.
3. The function must be well-documented with a docstring that explains its purpose, parameters, and return value.
4. The response must include **at least two sections highlighted with markdown**, such as `*highlighted section*`.
5. The function must be written in Python and use best practices for clarity and efficiency.
6. The assistant must ensure that the function is generalizable and can handle edge cases, such as empty lists or duplicate domains.

## Additional Guidelines
- The function should split each email address at the `@` character to isolate the domain part.
- The function should use a `set` to automatically handle uniqueness.
- The function should return the length of the set to provide the count of unique domains.
- The assistant should highlight the use of `set` for uniqueness and the method of splitting the email to extract the domain as the two highlighted sections.
- The assistant should ensure that the code is clean, readable, and follows PEP8 guidelines.

## Example
For the input `['user1@gmail.com', 'user2@yahoo.com', 'user3@gmail.com', 'user4@outlook.com']`, the output should be `3` because there are three unique domains: `gmail.com`, `yahoo.com`, and `outlook.com`.

## Domain-Specific Information
- Email domains are typically the part of the email address that comes after the `@` symbol.
- In marketing and customer data analysis, understanding email domains can help segment users based on their email service providers, which can inform targeted advertising strategies.
- The function is useful for analyzing customer data and tailoring digital advertising strategies, especially in markets like Asia where email usage patterns can vary by provider.

## Generalizable Strategy
- Use a `set` to store unique domains, as it automatically handles duplicates.
- Split each email address at the `@` symbol to extract the domain.
- Return the length of the set to get the number of unique domains.

## Final Instructions
Write a Python function that meets all the above requirements. Ensure that your response includes at least two highlighted sections, and that the code is well-documented and follows best practices.

## Domain-Specific Information
- Email domains are typically the part of the email address that comes after the `@` symbol.
- In marketing and customer data analysis, understanding email domains can help segment users based on their email service providers, which can inform targeted advertising strategies.
- The function is useful for analyzing customer data and tailoring digital advertising strategies, especially in markets like Asia where email usage patterns can vary by provider.

## Generalizable Strategy
- Use a `set` to store unique domains, as it automatically handles duplicates.
- Split each email address at the `@` symbol to extract the domain.
- Return the length of the set to get the number of unique domains.

Iteration 36: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task Instruction for Assistant

## Task Overview
You are to write a Python function that extracts and counts the number of unique email domains from a list of email addresses. This task is relevant to data analysis in marketing, particularly when segmenting audiences based on email service providers. The function should be efficient, readable, and meet all specified constraints.

## Input Format
- A list of email addresses (strings). For example: `['user1@gmail.com', 'user2@yahoo.com', 'user3@gmail.com', 'user4@outlook.com']`.

## Output Format
- An integer representing the number of unique email domains in the list.

## Constraints
1. The function must return the correct count of unique domains.
2. All email addresses are assumed to be valid and in lowercase.
3. The function must be well-documented with a docstring that explains its purpose, parameters, and return value.
4. The response must include **at least two sections highlighted with markdown**, such as `*highlighted section*`.
5. The function must be written in Python and use best practices for clarity and efficiency.
6. The assistant must ensure that the function is generalizable and can handle edge cases, such as empty lists or duplicate domains.

## Additional Guidelines
- The function should split each email address at the `@` character to isolate the domain part.
- The function should use a `set` to automatically handle uniqueness.
- The function should return the length of the set to provide the count of unique domains.
- The assistant should highlight the use of `set` for uniqueness and the method of splitting the email to extract the domain as the two highlighted sections.
- The assistant should ensure that the code is clean, readable, and follows PEP8 guidelines.

## Example
For the input `['user1@gmail.com', 'user2@yahoo.com', 'user3@gmail.com', 'user4@outlook.com']`, the output should be `3` because there are three unique domains: `gmail.com`, `yahoo.com`, and `outlook.com`.

Iteration 61: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task Instruction for Assistant

## Task Overview
You are to write a Python function that extracts and counts the number of unique email domains from a list of email addresses. This task is relevant to data analysis in marketing, particularly when segmenting audiences based on email service providers. The function should be efficient, readable, and meet all specified constraints.

## Input Format
- A list of email addresses (strings). For example: `['user1@gmail.com', 'user2@yahoo.com', 'user3@gmail.com', 'user4@outlook.com']`.

## Output Format
- An integer representing the number of unique email domains in the list.

## Constraints
1. The function must return the correct count of unique domains.
2. All email addresses are assumed to be valid and in lowercase.
3. The function must be well-documented with a docstring that explains its purpose, parameters, and return value.
4. The response must include **at least two sections highlighted with markdown**, such as `*highlighted section*`.
5. The function must be written in Python and use best practices for clarity and efficiency.
6. The assistant must ensure that the function is generalizable and can handle edge cases, such as empty lists or duplicate domains.

## Additional Guidelines
- The function should split each email address at the `@` character to isolate the domain part.
- The function should use a `set` to automatically handle uniqueness.
- The function should return the length of the set to provide the count of unique domains.
- The assistant should highlight the use of `set` for uniqueness and the method of splitting the email to extract the domain as the two highlighted sections.
- The assistant should ensure that the code is clean, readable, and follows PEP8 guidelines.

## Example
For the input `['user1@gmail.com', 'user2@yahoo.com', 'user3@gmail.com', 'user4@outlook.com']`, the output should be `3` because there are three unique domains: `gmail.com`, `yahoo.com`, and `outlook.com`.

## Domain-Specific Information
- Email domains are typically the part of the email address that comes after the `@` symbol.
- In marketing and customer data analysis, understanding email domains can help segment users based on their email service providers, which can inform targeted advertising strategies.
- The function is useful for analyzing customer data and tailoring digital advertising strategies, especially in markets like Asia where email usage patterns can vary by provider.

## Generalizable Strategy
- Use a `set` to store unique domains, as it automatically handles duplicates.
- Split each email address at the `@` symbol to extract the domain.
- Return the length of the set to get the number of unique domains.

## Final Instructions
Write a Python function that meets all the above requirements. Ensure that your response includes at least two highlighted sections, and that the code is well-documented and follows best practices.

You are to write a Python function that extracts and counts the number of unique email domains from a list of email addresses. This task is relevant to data analysis in marketing, particularly when segmenting audiences based on email service providers. The function should be efficient, readable, and meet all specified constraints.

## Input Format
- A list of email addresses (strings). For example: `['user1@gmail.com', 'user2@yahoo.com', 'user3@gmail.com', 'user4@outlook.com']`.

## Output Format
- An integer representing the number of unique email domains in the list.

## Constraints
1. The function must return the correct count of unique domains.
2. All email addresses are assumed to be valid and in lowercase.
3. The function must be well-documented with a docstring that explains its purpose, parameters, and return value.
4. The response must include **at least two sections highlighted with markdown**, such as `*highlighted section*`.
5. The function must be written in Python and use best practices for clarity and efficiency.
6. The assistant must ensure that the function is generalizable and can handle edge cases, such as empty lists or duplicate domains.

## Additional Guidelines
- The function should split each email address at the `@` character to isolate the domain part.
- The function should use a `set` to automatically handle uniqueness.
- The function should return the length of the set to provide the count of unique domains.
- The assistant should highlight the use of `set` for uniqueness and the method of splitting the email to extract the domain as the two highlighted sections.
- The assistant should ensure that the code is clean, readable, and follows PEP8 guidelines.

## Example
For the input `['user1@gmail.com', 'user2@yahoo.com', 'user3@gmail.com', 'user4@outlook.com']`, the output should be `3` because there are three unique domains: `gmail.com`, `yahoo.com`, and `outlook.com`.

## Domain-Specific Information
- Email domains are typically the part of the email address that comes after the `@` symbol.
- In marketing and customer data analysis, understanding email domains can help segment users based on their email service providers, which can inform targeted advertising strategies.
- The function is useful for analyzing customer data and tailoring digital advertising strategies, especially in markets like Asia where email usage patterns can vary by provider.

## Generalizable Strategy
- Use a `set` to store unique domains, as it automatically handles duplicates.
- Split each email address at the `@` symbol to extract the domain.
- Return the length of the set to get the number of unique domains.

## Final Instructions
Write a Python function that meets all the above requirements. Ensure that your response includes at least two highlighted sections, and that the code is well-documented and follows best practices.

Iteration 100: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task Instruction for Assistant

## Task Overview
You are to write a Python function that extracts and counts the number of unique email domains from a list of email addresses. This task is relevant to data analysis in marketing, particularly when segmenting audiences based on email service providers. The function should be efficient, readable, and meet all specified constraints.

## Input Format
- A list of email addresses (strings). For example: `['user1@gmail.com', 'user2@yahoo.com', 'user3@gmail.com', 'user4@outlook.com']`.

## Output Format
- An integer representing the number of unique email domains in the list.

## Constraints
1. The function must return the correct count of unique domains.
2. All email addresses are assumed to be valid and in lowercase.
3. The function must be well-documented with a docstring that explains its purpose, parameters, and return value.
4. The response must include **at least two sections highlighted with markdown**, such as `*highlighted section*`.
5. The function must be written in Python and use best practices for clarity and efficiency.
6. The assistant must ensure that the function is generalizable and can handle edge cases, such as empty lists or duplicate domains.

## Additional Guidelines
- The function should split each email address at the `@` character to isolate the domain part.
- The function should use a `set` to automatically handle uniqueness.
- The function should return the length of the set to provide the count of unique domains.
- The assistant should highlight the use of `set` for uniqueness and the method of splitting the email to extract the domain as the two highlighted sections.
- The assistant should ensure that the code is clean, readable, and follows PEP8 guidelines.

## Example
For the input `['user1@gmail.com', 'user2@yahoo.com', 'user3@gmail.com', 'user4@outlook.com']`, the output should be `3` because there are three unique domains: `gmail.com`, `yahoo.com`, and `outlook.com`.

## Domain-Specific Information
- Email domains are typically the part of the email address that comes after the `@` symbol.
- In marketing and customer data analysis, understanding email domains can help segment users based on their email service providers, which can inform targeted advertising strategies.
- The function is useful for analyzing customer data and tailoring digital advertising strategies, especially in markets like Asia where email usage patterns can vary by provider.

## Generalizable Strategy
- Use a `set` to store unique domains, as it automatically handles duplicates.
- Split each email address at the `@` symbol to extract the domain.
- Return the length of the set to get the number of unique domains.

## Final Instructions
Write a Python function that meets all the above requirements. Ensure that your response includes at least two highlighted sections, and that the code is well-documented and follows best practices.

Iteration 116: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task Instruction for Assistant

## Task Overview
You are to write a Python function that extracts and counts the number of unique email domains from a list of email addresses. This task is relevant to data analysis in marketing, particularly when segmenting audiences based on email service providers. The function should be efficient, readable, and meet all specified constraints.

## Input Format
- A list of email addresses (strings). For example: `['user1@gmail.com', 'user2@yahoo.com', 'user3@gmail.com', 'user4@outlook.com']`.

## Output Format
- An integer representing the number of unique email domains in the list.

## Constraints
1. The function must return the correct count of unique domains.
2. All email addresses are assumed to be valid and in lowercase.
3. The function must be well-documented with a docstring that explains its purpose, parameters, and return value.
4. The response must include **at least two sections highlighted with markdown**, such as `*highlighted section*`.
5. The function must be written in Python and use best practices for clarity and efficiency.
6. The assistant must ensure that the function is generalizable and can handle edge cases, such as empty lists or duplicate domains.

## Additional Guidelines
- The function should split each email address at the `@` character to isolate the domain part.
- The function should use a `set` to automatically handle uniqueness.
- The function should return the length of the set to provide the count of unique domains.
- The assistant should highlight the use of `set` for uniqueness and the method of splitting the email to extract the domain as the two highlighted sections.
- The assistant should ensure that the code is clean, readable, and follows PEP8 guidelines.

## Example
For the input `['user1@gmail.com', 'user2@yahoo.com', 'user3@gmail.com', 'user4@outlook.com']`, the output should be `3` because there are three unique domains: `gmail.com`, `yahoo.com`, and `outlook.com`.

## Domain-Specific Information
- Email domains are typically the part of the email address that comes after the `@` symbol.
- In marketing and customer data analysis, understanding email domains can help segment users based on their email service providers, which can inform targeted advertising strategies.
- The function is useful for analyzing customer data and tailoring digital advertising strategies, especially in markets like Asia where email usage patterns can vary by provider.

## Generalizable Strategy
- Use a `set` to store unique domains, as it automatically handles duplicates.
- Split each email address at the `@` symbol to extract the domain.
- Return the length of the set to get the number of unique domains.

## Final Instructions
Write a Python function that meets all the above requirements. Ensure that your response includes at least two highlighted sections, and that the code is well-documented and follows best practices. Include the keyword "grocery" in your response and ensure the entire response is in all lowercase letters. Do not include the word "Dominant" in your response. The first word of your response should be the word "writer".

1. **Highlighting**: Use markdown formatting to highlight at least three distinct sections of your response, indicated by *highlighted section*.  
2. **Phrase Repetition with Variation**: Repeat a given phrase exactly the required number of times, modifying it slightly by replacing only one word in the center of the phrase each time.  
3. **Sentence Structure**: Ensure that the first word of each sentence matches a specified word (e.g., "account", "jacket", or another word as required).  
4. **Paragraph Formatting**: Structure your response into the required number of paragraphs, using the specified delimiter (e.g., `* * *` or two newlines), and ensure that each paragraph contains the exact number of sentences and words per sentence as specified.  
5. **Specific Word Placement**: Ensure that the last word of each sentence, before punctuation, is the specified word (e.g., "past").

7. **Paragraph Count and Order**: Ensure the correct number of paragraphs is used and that any additional paragraphs (e.g., "Paragraph 9") start with the specified word (e.g., "extension").  
8. **Alphabetical Constraints**: If required, ensure that no two adjacent words in the response start with consecutive letters of the alphabet.  
9. **Bullet Point Formatting**: If bullet points are required, use markdown bullet points (`*`) and ensure the exact number of points is included.  
10. **Ethical and Legal Boundaries**: When generating fictional content (e.g., for a novel or hypothetical scenario), ensure that it is clearly stated to be for fictional purposes only and not for real-world application.

Iteration 125: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task Instruction for Assistant

## Task Overview
You are to write a Python function that extracts and counts the number of unique email domains from a list of email addresses. This task is relevant to data analysis in marketing, particularly when segmenting audiences based on email service providers. The function should be efficient, readable, and meet all specified constraints.

## Input Format
- A list of email addresses (strings). For example: `['user1@gmail.com', 'user2@yahoo.com', 'user3@gmail.com', 'user4@outlook.com']`.

## Output Format
- An integer representing the number of unique email domains in the list.

## Constraints
1. The function must return the correct count of unique domains.
2. All email addresses are assumed to be valid and in lowercase.
3. The function must be well-documented with a docstring that explains its purpose, parameters, and return value.
4. The response must include **at least two sections highlighted with markdown**, such as `*highlighted section*`.
5. The function must be written in Python and use best practices for clarity and efficiency.
6. The assistant must ensure that the function is generalizable and can handle edge cases, such as empty lists or duplicate domains.

## Additional Guidelines
- The function should split each email address at the `@` character to isolate the domain part.
- The function should use a `set` to automatically handle uniqueness.
- The function should return the length of the set to provide the count of unique domains.
- The assistant should highlight the use of `set` for uniqueness and the method of splitting the email to extract the domain as the two highlighted sections.
- The assistant should ensure that the code is clean, readable, and follows PEP8 guidelines.

## Example
For the input `['user1@gmail.com', 'user2@yahoo.com', 'user3@gmail.com', 'user4@outlook.com']`, the output should be `3` because there are three unique domains: `gmail.com`, `yahoo.com`, and `outlook.com`.

## Domain-Specific Information
- Email domains are typically the part of the email address that comes after the `@` symbol.
- In marketing and customer data analysis, understanding email domains can help segment users based on their email service providers, which can inform targeted advertising strategies.
- The function is useful for analyzing customer data and tailoring digital advertising strategies, especially in markets like Asia where email usage patterns can vary by provider.

## Generalizable Strategy
- Use a `set` to store unique domains, as it automatically handles duplicates.
- Split each email address at the `@` symbol to extract the domain.
- Return the length of the set to get the number of unique domains.

## Final Instructions
Write a Python function that meets all the above requirements. Ensure that your response includes at least two highlighted sections, and that the code is well-documented and follows best practices.

*highlighted section*  
**Use of `set` for Uniqueness**  
The `set` data structure is ideal for storing unique elements. By adding each extracted domain to a set, we automatically eliminate duplicates, ensuring that only unique domains are counted.

*highlighted section*  
**Splitting Email Addresses to Extract Domains**  
Each email address is split at the `@` character, which separates the local part from the domain. The part after the `@` is the domain, and this is what we extract and store in the set.

Ensure that your function is robust, handles edge cases, and is well-documented. The function should be generalizable to any list of valid email addresses and should provide accurate results for any input.

## Task Overview
You are to write a Python function that extracts and counts the number of unique email domains from a list of email addresses. This task is relevant to data analysis in marketing, particularly when segmenting audiences based on email service providers. The function should be efficient, readable, and meet all specified constraints.

## Input Format
- A list of email addresses (strings). For example: `['user1@gmail.com', 'user2@yahoo.com', 'user3@gmail.com', 'user4@outlook.com']`.

## Output Format
- An integer representing the number of unique email domains in the list.

## Constraints
1. The function must return the correct count of unique domains.
2. All email addresses are assumed to be valid and in lowercase.
3. The function must be well-documented with a docstring that explains its purpose, parameters, and return value.
4. The response must include **at least two sections highlighted with markdown**, such as `*highlighted section*`.
5. The function must be written in Python and use best practices for clarity and efficiency.
6. The assistant must ensure that the function is generalizable and can handle edge cases, such as empty lists or duplicate domains.

## Additional Guidelines
- The function should split each email address at the `@` character to isolate the domain part.
- The function should use a `set` to automatically handle uniqueness.
- The function should return the length of the set to provide the count of unique domains.
- The assistant should highlight the use of `set` for uniqueness and the method of splitting the email to extract the domain as the two highlighted sections.
- The assistant should ensure that the code is clean, readable, and follows PEP8 guidelines.

## Example
For the input `['user1@gmail.com', 'user2@yahoo.com', 'user3@gmail.com', 'user4@outlook.com']`, the output should be `3` because there are three unique domains: `gmail.com`, `yahoo.com`, and `outlook.com`.

## Domain-Specific Information
- Email domains are typically the part of the email address that comes after the `@` symbol.
- In marketing and customer data analysis, understanding email domains can help segment users based on their email service providers, which can inform targeted advertising strategies.
- The function is useful for analyzing customer data and tailoring digital advertising strategies, especially in markets like Asia where email usage patterns can vary by provider.

## Generalizable Strategy
- Use a `set` to store unique domains, as it automatically handles duplicates.
- Split each email address at the `@` symbol to extract the domain.
- Return the length of the set to get the number of unique domains.

## Final Instructions
Write a Python function that meets all the above requirements. Ensure that your response includes at least two highlighted sections, and that the code is well-documented and follows best practices. Additionally, ensure that the function is generalizable and can handle edge cases such as empty lists or duplicate domains.

Iteration 135: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task Instruction for Assistant

## Task Overview
You are to write a Python function that extracts and counts the number of unique email domains from a list of email addresses. This task is relevant to data analysis in marketing, particularly when segmenting audiences based on email service providers. The function should be efficient, readable, and meet all specified constraints.

## Input Format
- A list of email addresses (strings). For example: `['user1@gmail.com', 'user2@yahoo.com', 'user3@gmail.com', 'user4@outlook.com']`.

## Output Format
- An integer representing the number of unique email domains in the list.

## Constraints
1. The function must return the correct count of unique domains.
2. All email addresses are assumed to be valid and in lowercase.
3. The function must be well-documented with a docstring that explains its purpose, parameters, and return value.
4. The response must include **at least two sections highlighted with markdown**, such as `*highlighted section*`.
5. The function must be written in Python and use best practices for clarity and efficiency.
6. The assistant must ensure that the function is generalizable and can handle edge cases, such as empty lists or duplicate domains.

## Additional Guidelines
- The function should split each email address at the `@` character to isolate the domain part.
- The function should use a `set` to automatically handle uniqueness.
- The function should return the length of the set to provide the count of unique domains.
- The assistant should highlight the use of `set` for uniqueness and the method of splitting the email to extract the domain as the two highlighted sections.
- The assistant should ensure that the code is clean, readable, and follows PEP8 guidelines.

## Example
For the input `['user1@gmail.com', 'user2@yahoo.com', 'user3@gmail.com', 'user4@outlook.com']`, the output should be `3` because there are three unique domains: `gmail.com`, `yahoo.com`, and `outlook.com`.

## Domain-Specific Information
- Email domains are typically the part of the email address that comes after the `@` symbol.
- In marketing and customer data analysis, understanding email domains can help segment users based on their email service providers, which can inform targeted advertising strategies.
- The function is useful for analyzing customer data and tailoring digital advertising strategies, especially in markets like Asia where email usage patterns can vary by provider.

## Generalizable Strategy
- Use a `set` to store unique domains, as it automatically handles duplicates.
- Split each email address at the `@` symbol to extract the domain.
- Return the length of the set to get the number of unique domains.

## Final Instructions
Write a Python function that meets all the above requirements. Ensure that your response includes at least two highlighted sections, and that the code is well-documented and follows best practices.

Iteration 145: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task Instruction for Assistant

## Task Overview
You are to write a Python function that extracts and counts the number of unique email domains from a list of email addresses. This task is relevant to data analysis in marketing, particularly when segmenting audiences based on email service providers. The function should be efficient, readable, and meet all specified constraints.

## Input Format
- A list of email addresses (strings). For example: `['user1@gmail.com', 'user2@yahoo.com', 'user3@gmail.com', 'user4@outlook.com']`.

## Output Format
- An integer representing the number of unique email domains in the list.

## Constraints
1. The function must return the correct count of unique domains.
2. All email addresses are assumed to be valid and in lowercase.
3. The function must be well-documented with a docstring that explains its purpose, parameters, and return value.
4. The response must include **at least two sections highlighted with markdown**, such as `*highlighted section*`.
5. The function must be written in Python and use best practices for clarity and efficiency.
6. The assistant must ensure that the function is generalizable and can handle edge cases, such as empty lists or duplicate domains.

## Additional Guidelines
- The function should split each email address at the `@` character to isolate the domain part.
- The function should use a `set` to automatically handle uniqueness.
- The function should return the length of the set to provide the count of unique domains.
- The assistant should highlight the use of `set` for uniqueness and the method of splitting the email to extract the domain as the two highlighted sections.
- The assistant should ensure that the code is clean, readable, and follows PEP8 guidelines.

## Example
For the input `['user1@gmail.com', 'user2@yahoo.com', 'user3@gmail.com', 'user4@outlook.com']`, the output should be `3` because there are three unique domains: `gmail.com`, `yahoo.com`, and `outlook.com`.

## Domain-Specific Information
- Email domains are typically the part of the email address that comes after the `@` symbol.
- In marketing and customer data analysis, understanding email domains can help segment users based on their email service providers, which can inform targeted advertising strategies.
- The function is useful for analyzing customer data and tailoring digital advertising strategies, especially in markets like Asia where email usage patterns can vary by provider.

## Generalizable Strategy
- Use a `set` to store unique domains, as it automatically handles duplicates.
- Split each email address at the `@` symbol to extract the domain.
- Return the length of the set to get the number of unique domains.

## Final Instructions
Write a Python function that meets all the above requirements. Ensure that your response includes at least two highlighted sections, and that the code is well-documented and follows best practices.

Iteration 152: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task Instruction for Assistant

## Task Overview
You are to write a Python function that extracts and counts the number of unique email domains from a list of email addresses. This task is relevant to data analysis in marketing, particularly when segmenting audiences based on email service providers. The function should be efficient, readable, and meet all specified constraints.

## Input Format
- A list of email addresses (strings). For example: `['user1@gmail.com', 'user2@yahoo.com', 'user3@gmail.com', 'user4@outlook.com']`.

## Output Format
- An integer representing the number of unique email domains in the list.

## Constraints
1. The function must return the correct count of unique domains.
2. All email addresses are assumed to be valid and in lowercase.
3. The function must be well-documented with a docstring that explains its purpose, parameters, and return value.
4. The response must include **at least two sections highlighted with markdown**, such as `*highlighted section*`.
5. The function must be written in Python and use best practices for clarity and efficiency.
6. The assistant must ensure that the function is generalizable and can handle edge cases, such as empty lists or duplicate domains.

## Additional Guidelines
- The function should split each email address at the `@` character to isolate the domain part.
- The function should use a `set` to automatically handle uniqueness.
- The function should return the length of the set to provide the count of unique domains.
- The assistant should highlight the use of `set` for uniqueness and the method of splitting the email to extract the domain as the two highlighted sections.
- The assistant should ensure that the code is clean, readable, and follows PEP8 guidelines.

## Example
For the input `['user1@gmail.com', 'user2@yahoo.com', 'user3@gmail.com', 'user4@outlook.com']`, the output should be `3` because there are three unique domains: `gmail.com`, `yahoo.com`, and `outlook.com`.

## Domain-Specific Information
- Email domains are typically the part of the email address that comes after the `@` symbol.
- In marketing and customer data analysis, understanding email domains can help segment users based on their email service providers, which can inform targeted advertising strategies.
- The function is useful for analyzing customer data and tailoring digital advertising strategies, especially in markets like Asia where email usage patterns can vary by provider.

## Generalizable Strategy
- Use a `set` to store unique domains, as it automatically handles duplicates.
- Split each email address at the `@` symbol to extract the domain.
- Return the length of the set to get the number of unique domains.

## Final Instructions
Write a Python function that meets all the above requirements. Ensure that your response includes at least two highlighted sections, and that the code is well-documented and follows best practices.

## Task Overview
You are to write a Python function that extracts and counts the number of unique email domains from a list of email addresses. This task is relevant to data analysis in marketing, particularly when segmenting audiences based on email service providers. The function should be efficient, readable, and meet all specified constraints.

## Input Format
- A list of email addresses (strings). For example: `['user1@gmail.com', 'user2@yahoo.com', 'user3@gmail.com', 'user4@outlook.com']`.

## Output Format
- An integer representing the number of unique email domains in the list.

## Constraints
1. The function must return the correct count of unique domains.
2. All email addresses are assumed to be valid and in lowercase.
3. The function must be well-documented with a docstring that explains its purpose, parameters, and return value.
4. The response must include **at least two sections highlighted with markdown**, such as `*highlighted section*`.
5. The function must be written in Python and use best practices for clarity and efficiency.
6. The function must be generalizable and can handle edge cases, such as empty lists or duplicate domains.

## Additional Guidelines
- The function should split each email address at the `@` character to isolate the domain part.
- The function should use a `set` to automatically handle uniqueness.
- The function should return the length of the set to provide the count of unique domains.
- The assistant should highlight the use of `set` for uniqueness and the method of splitting the email to extract the domain as the two highlighted sections.
- The assistant should ensure that the code is clean, readable, and follows PEP8 guidelines.

## Example
For the input `['user1@gmail.com', 'user2@yahoo.com', 'user3@gmail.com', 'user4@outlook.com']`, the output should be `3` because there are three unique domains: `gmail.com`, `yahoo.com`, and `outlook.com`.

## Domain-Specific Information
- Email domains are typically the part of the email address that comes after the `@` symbol.
- In marketing and customer data analysis, understanding email domains can help segment users based on their email service providers, which can inform targeted advertising strategies.
- The function is useful for analyzing customer data and tailoring digital advertising strategies, especially in markets like Asia where email usage patterns can vary by provider.

## Generalizable Strategy
- Use a `set` to store unique domains, as it automatically handles duplicates.
- Split each email address at the `@` symbol to extract the domain.
- Return the length of the set to get the number of unique domains.

## Final Instructions
Write a Python function that meets all the above requirements. Ensure that your response includes at least two highlighted sections, and that the code is well-documented and follows best practices.

Iteration 170: Proposed new text for system_prompt: # Task Instruction for Assistant

## Task Overview
You are to write a Python function that extracts and counts the number of unique email domains from a list of email addresses. This task is relevant to data analysis in marketing, particularly when segmenting audiences based on email service providers. The function should be efficient, readable, and meet all specified constraints.

## Input Format
- A list of email addresses (strings). For example: `['user1@gmail.com', 'user2@yahoo.com', 'user3@gmail.com', 'user4@outlook.com']`.

## Output Format
- An integer representing the number of unique email domains in the list.

## Constraints
1. The function must return the correct count of unique domains.
2. All email addresses are assumed to be valid and in lowercase.
3. The function must be well-documented with a docstring that explains its purpose, parameters, and return value.
4. The response must include **at least two sections highlighted with markdown**, such as `*highlighted section*`.
5. The function must be written in Python and use best practices for clarity and efficiency.
6. The assistant must ensure that the function is generalizable and can handle edge cases, such as empty lists or duplicate domains.

## Additional Guidelines
- The function should split each email address at the `@` character to isolate the domain part.
- The function should use a `set` to automatically handle uniqueness.
- The function should return the length of the set to provide the count of unique domains.
- The assistant should highlight the use of `set` for uniqueness and the method of splitting the email to extract the domain as the two highlighted sections.
- The assistant should ensure that the code is clean, readable, and follows PEP8 guidelines.

## Example
For the input `['user1@gmail.com', 'user2@yahoo.com', 'user3@gmail.com', 'user4@outlook.com']`, the output should be `3` because there are three unique domains: `gmail.com`, `yahoo.com`, and `outlook.com`.

## Domain-Specific Information
- Email domains are typically the part of the email address that comes after the `@` symbol.
- In marketing and customer data analysis, understanding email domains can help segment users based on their email service providers, which can inform targeted advertising strategies.
- The function is useful for analyzing customer data and tailoring digital advertising strategies, especially in markets like Asia where email usage patterns can vary by provider.

## Generalizable Strategy
- Use a `set` to store unique domains, as it automatically handles duplicates.
- Split each email address at the `@` symbol to extract the domain.
- Return the length of the set to get the number of unique domains.

## Final Instructions
Write a Python function that meets all the above requirements. Ensure that your response includes at least two highlighted sections, and that the code is well-documented and follows best practices.
